[2025-12-10T11:22:18Z] Lzafeer Ahmad B F: After the episode aired, numerous people used the eponymous figures (4, 8, 15, 16, 23 and 42) as lottery entries. According to the Pittsburgh Tribune-Review, within three days, the numbers were tried over 500 times by local players.[6] Likewise, in the same period, over 200 people in Michigan alone used the sequence for the Mega Millions lottery[7] and by October, thousands had tried them for the multi-state Powerball lottery.[8][9] The issue came to attention after a Mega Millions drawing for a near-record US$380,000,000 jackpot on January 4, 2011 drew a series of numbers in which the three lowest numbers (4-8-15) and the mega ball (42) matched four of the five numbers. The #42 is also the "Mega Number" in Hurley's "Mega Lotto" ticket. The players who played the combination won $150 each (or $118 in California).[10] ↵ In May 2024, Mega-Sena, the largest lottery in Brazil, drew a series in which five numbers (8, 15, 16, 23 and 42) matched the sequence. A total of 2,967 players won a prize of R$ 1,878.49 each (roughly $360 in May 2024 figures)

[2025-12-11T06:14:32Z] Pavan Pamidimarri: 12.	Benoy Basu, Badal Gupta, and Dinesh Gupta were teenage revolutionaries who attacked X in Dalhousie Square in Kolkata in December 1930. Dressed in European clothes, they entered X and killed Lt. Col. Simpson, the Inspector General of Prisons, who was notorious for his oppression of prisoners. X was the heart of the colonial administration in Kolkata, so they conducted this assassination there to send a clear message that no place is impenetrable for Indian revolutionaries. After killing Simpson, they refused to surrender; Badal took cyanide and the other two shot themselves. After independence, Dalhousie Square was renamed to Y. The picture shows statues of the trio in front of X. ID X and Y. ‎image omitted

Lisbon’s famous black-and-white cobblestones — "calçada portuguesa" — aren’t just pavement.... they’re a handmade public art tradition. During the age of Portuguese influence, the style spread to: ↵ -Brazil (most famously Rio’s Copacabana promenade) ↵ -Macau ↵ -Cape Verde ↵ -Mozambique ↵ Each region adopted its own motifs, but the technique remained distinctly Portuguese. ↵ The tradition began after the 1755 Great Lisbon Earthquake, when the city had to be rebuilt. But the distinctive patterned pavements appeared in the mid 1800s, when the military governor ordered prisoners to pave the castle’s courtyard with a patterned design using locally quarried limestone. ↵ The result was so striking that Lisbon’s city council commissioned more. ↵ This first pattern was known as the XY, with an iconic wave in the open sea motif. ↵ We know the term XY for a slightly different context nowadays... [2025-12-11T19:48:23Z] AntNishu: Q. In indian film industry of early 1900s, deep social taboos prevented women from the dominant communities from appearing in movies. directors struggled to fill female roles, often resorting to casting male actors (lead female role of Taramati in Raja Harishchandra was played by a male actor Anna Salunke) ↵ Facing this vacuum, a very small but notably progressive community stepped forward. Women from this group showed remarkable courage, taking on the leading female roles and effectively becoming the foremothers of indian cinema. Their groundbreaking work on the big screen shattered existing taboos and paved the way for women from all communities to eventually join the industry. India's first ever miss india was a woman from this very same pioneering group. ID this community.
